SIZE="2"><B>February&nbsp;25, 2009 </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>10:00 a.m. Pacific Standard Time </B></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">To Holders of Common Stock of Apple Inc.: </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Notice is hereby
given that the 2009 annual meeting of shareholders (the &#147;<I>Annual Meeting</I>&#148;) of Apple Inc., a California corporation (the &#147;<I>Company</I>&#148;), will be held on Wednesday, February&nbsp;25, 2009 at 10:00 a.m. Pacific Standard
Time, in Building 4 of the Company&#146;s principal executive offices located at the address shown above for the following purposes, as more fully described in the accompanying proxy statement (the &#147;<I>Proxy Statement</I>&#148;): </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>

<TD WIDTH="4%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">1.</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">To elect the Company&#146;s Board of Directors (the &#147;<I>Board</I>&#148;). The Board intends to present for election the following eight nominees, all of whom are current
directors of the Company: William V. Campbell, Millard S. Drexler, Albert A. Gore, Jr., Steven P. Jobs, Andrea Jung, Arthur D. Levinson, Ph.D., Eric E. Schmidt, Ph.D. and Jerome B. York; </FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P
STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">To transact such other business as may properly come before the Annual Meeting and any postponement(s) or adjournment(s) thereof. </FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Only shareholders of record as of the close of business on December&nbsp;29, 2008 are entitled to receive notice of, to attend and to vote at the Annual
Meeting. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Company is pleased to continue to take advantage of the Securities and Exchange Commission (the &#147;<I>SEC</I>&#148;) rules
that allow issuers to furnish proxy materials to their shareholders on the Internet. The Company believes these rules allow it to provide you with the information you need while lowering the costs of delivery and reducing the environmental impact of
the Annual Meeting. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">You are cordially invited to attend the Annual Meeting in person. However, to ensure that your vote is counted at the

(408)&nbsp;996-1010. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Why did I receive a one-page notice in the mail regarding the Internet availability of proxy materials this year instead of a full
set of proxy materials? </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Pursuant to rules adopted by the SEC, the Company has elected to provide access to its proxy materials over the
Internet. Accordingly, the Company is sending a Notice of Internet Availability of Proxy Materials (the &#147;<I>Notice</I>&#148;) to the Company&#146;s shareholders of record and beneficial owners. All shareholders will have the ability to access
the proxy materials on the website referred to in the Notice or request to receive a printed set of the proxy materials. Instructions on how to access the proxy materials over the Internet or to request a printed copy may be found in the Notice. In
addition, shareholders may request to receive proxy materials in printed form by mail or electronically by email on an ongoing basis. The Company encourages you to take advantage of the availability of the proxy materials on the Internet in order to
help reduce the environmental impact of the Annual Meeting. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>I share an address with another shareholder, and we received only one paper copy of the
proxy materials. How may I obtain an additional copy of the proxy materials? </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Company has adopted a procedure called
&#147;householding,&#148; which the SEC has approved. Under this procedure, the Company is delivering a single copy of the Notice and, if applicable, this Proxy Statement and the Annual Report to multiple shareholders who share the same address
unless the Company has received contrary instructions from one or more of the shareholders. This procedure reduces the Company&#146;s printing costs, mailing costs and fees. Shareholders who participate in householding will continue to be able to
access and receive separate proxy cards. Upon written or oral request, the Company will deliver promptly a separate copy of the Notice and, if applicable, this Proxy Statement and the Annual Report to any shareholder at a shared address to which the
Company delivered a single copy of any of these documents. To receive a separate copy of the Notice and, if applicable, this Proxy Statement or the Annual Report, shareholders may write or call the Company at the following address and telephone
number: </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Investor Relations </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">1
Infinite Loop MS 301-4IR </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Cupertino, California 95014 </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT

</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Each share of the Company&#146;s common stock has one vote on each matter. As of December&nbsp;10, 2008, there were 889,485,436 shares
of the Company&#146;s common stock issued and outstanding, held by 30,706 holders of record. Only shareholders of record as of the close of business on December&nbsp;29, 2008 (the &#147;<I>Record Date</I>&#148;) are entitled to receive notice of, to
attend, and to vote at the Annual Meeting. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>What is the difference between a shareholder of record and a beneficial owner of shares held in street name?
</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>Shareholder of Record</I>. If your shares are registered directly in your name with the Company&#146;s transfer agent, Computershare
Investor Services, LLC (&#147;<I>Computershare</I>&#148;), you are considered the shareholder of record with respect to those shares, and the Notice was sent directly to you by the Company. If you request printed copies of the proxy materials by
mail, you will receive a proxy card. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>Beneficial Owner of Shares Held in Street Name</I>. If your shares are held in an account at a
brokerage firm, bank, broker-dealer, or other similar organization, then you are the beneficial owner of shares held in &#147;street name,&#148; and the Notice was forwarded to you by that organization. The organization holding your account is
considered the shareholder of record for purposes of voting at the Annual Meeting. As a beneficial owner, you have the right to direct that organization on how to vote the shares held in your account. If you request printed copies of the proxy
materials by mail, you will receive a vote instruction form. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>If I am a shareholder of record of the Company&#146;s shares, how do I vote?
</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">There are four ways to vote: </FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>In person</I>. If you are a shareholder of record, you may vote in person at the Annual Meeting. The Company will give you a ballot when you arrive.
</FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>

is called a quorum. Your shares will be counted for purposes of determining if there is a quorum, whether representing votes for, against or abstained, if you: </FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>

STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>How are proxies voted? </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">All valid proxies received

shareholder&#146;s instructions. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>What happens if I do not give specific voting instructions? </B></FONT></P> <P

holders may determine in their discretion with respect to any other matters properly presented for a vote at the Annual Meeting. See the section entitled &#147;Other Matters&#148; below. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>Beneficial Owners of Shares Held in Street Name</I>. If you are a beneficial owner of shares held in street name and do not provide the organization
that holds your shares with specific voting instructions, under the rules of various national and regional securities exchanges, the organization that holds your shares may generally vote on routine matters but cannot vote on non-routine matters. If
the organization that holds your shares does not receive instructions from you on how to vote your shares on a non-routine matter, the organization that holds your shares will inform the inspector of election that it does not have the authority to
vote on this matter with respect to your shares. This is generally referred to as a &#147;broker non-vote.&#148; </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">4 </FONT></P>

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Who will serve as the inspector of election? </B></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">A representative from Computershare will serve as the inspector of election. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Which ballot measures are considered &#147;routine&#148; or &#147;non-routine&#148;? </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The election of
directors (Proposal No.&nbsp;1) is a matter the Company believes will be considered routine. A broker or other nominee may generally vote on routine matters, and therefore no broker non-votes are expected to exist in connection with Proposal
No.&nbsp;1. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Shareholder proposals (Proposals No.&nbsp;2, No.&nbsp;3, No.&nbsp;4 and No.&nbsp;5) are matters the Company believes will be
considered non-routine. A broker or other nominee cannot vote without instructions on non-routine matters, and therefore there may be broker non-votes on Proposals No.&nbsp;2, No.&nbsp;3, No.&nbsp;4 and No.&nbsp;5. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>How are broker non-votes treated? </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Broker non-votes
are counted for purposes of determining whether a quorum is present. For the purpose of determining whether the shareholders have approved all matters other than the election of directors (Proposal No.&nbsp;1), broker non-votes have the same effect
as an &#147;AGAINST&#148; vote. The Company encourages you to provide voting instructions to the organization that holds your shares by carefully following the instructions provided in the Notice. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>How are abstentions treated? </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Abstentions are counted
for purposes of determining whether a quorum is present. Shares not present at the Annual Meeting and abstentions have no effect on the election of directors (Proposal No.&nbsp;1). For the purpose of determining whether the shareholders have
approved all other matters, abstentions have the same effect as an &#147;AGAINST&#148; vote. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>What is the voting requirement to approve each of the
proposals? </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">For Proposal No.&nbsp;1, the eight nominees receiving the highest number of affirmative votes of the outstanding shares of
the Company&#146;s common stock present or represented by proxy and voting at the Annual Meeting will be elected as directors to serve until the next annual meeting of shareholders and until their successors are duly elected and qualified.
</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Approval of Proposals No.&nbsp;2, No.&nbsp;3, No.&nbsp;4, and No.&nbsp;5 requires a vote that satisfies the following two criteria:
</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">the affirmative vote must constitute a majority of the voting power present or represented by proxy and voting at the Annual Meeting; and
</FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>

STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Can I change my vote after I have voted? </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">You may
revoke your proxy and change your vote at any time before the final vote at the Annual Meeting. You may vote again on a later date via the Internet or by telephone (only your latest Internet or telephone proxy submitted prior to the Annual Meeting
will be counted), by signing and returning a new proxy card or vote instruction form with a later date, or by attending the Annual Meeting and voting in person. However, your attendance at the Annual Meeting will not automatically revoke your proxy
unless you vote again at the Annual Meeting or specifically request that your prior proxy be revoked by delivering to the Company&#146;s Corporate Secretary at 1 Infinite Loop, Cupertino, California 95014 a written notice of revocation prior to the
Annual Meeting. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>

<FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>Act</I>&#148;), which lists the requirements for the inclusion of shareholder proposals in company-sponsored proxy materials. Shareholder proposals must
be delivered to the Company&#146;s Corporate Secretary by mail at 1 Infinite Loop, Cupertino, California 95014 or by facsimile at (408)&nbsp;253-7457. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:4%"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>Requirements for Shareholder Proposals to be Brought Before the 2010 Annual Meeting of Shareholders</I>. Notice of any director nomination or other proposal that you intend to present at the 2010 annual meeting of
shareholders, but do not intend to have included in the proxy statement and form of proxy relating to the 2010 annual meeting of shareholders, must be delivered to the Company&#146;s Corporate Secretary by mail at 1 Infinite Loop, Cupertino,
California 95014 or by facsimile at (408)&nbsp;253-7457 not later than the close of business on November&nbsp;27, 2009 and not earlier than the close of business on October&nbsp;28, 2009. In addition, your notice must set forth the information
required by the Company&#146;s bylaws with respect to each director nomination or other proposal that you intend to present at the 2010 annual meeting of shareholders. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The proxy solicited by the Company for the 2010 annual meeting of shareholders will confer discretionary authority on the Company&#146;s proxies to vote on (i)&nbsp;any proposal presented by a shareholder at that
meeting for which the Company has not been provided with notice on or prior to November&nbsp;27, 2009 and (ii)&nbsp;any proposal made in accordance with the Company&#146;s bylaw provisions, if the proxy statement relating to the 2010 annual meeting
of shareholders briefly describes the matter and how the Company&#146;s proxies intend to vote on it, if the shareholder does not comply with the requirements of Rule 14a-4(c)(2) under the Exchange Act. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>

</B>joined Genentech, Inc. (&#147;<I>Genentech</I>&#148;) in 1980 and has been Chief Executive Officer and a director of Genentech since July 1995 and serves on the Executive Committee. Dr.&nbsp;Levinson has been Chairman of Genentech since
September 1999. Dr.&nbsp;Levinson also is a director of Google Inc. (&#147;<I>Google</I>&#148;), where he serves on the Leadership Development and Compensation Committee. In addition, Dr.&nbsp;Levinson serves on the Board of Scientific Consultants
of the Memorial Sloan-Kettering Cancer Center, on the Industrial Advisory Board of the California Institute for Quantitative Biomedical Research, on the Advisory Council for the Princeton University Department of Molecular Biology, on the Advisory

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Jerome B. York </B>has been Chief Executive Officer of Harwinton Capital LLC (formerly Harwinton
Capital Corporation), a private investment company that he controls, since September 2000. Mr.&nbsp;York also is a director of Dana Holding Corporation, where he serves on the Audit Committee and Compensation Committee, MyPublisher, Inc., and Tyco
International Ltd., where he serves on the Audit Committee. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Role of the Board; Corporate Governance Matters </B></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">It is the paramount duty of the Board to oversee the Company&#146;s Chief Executive Officer (the &#147;<I>CEO</I>&#148;) and other senior management in
the competent and ethical operation of the Company on a day-to-day basis and to assure that the long-term interests of the shareholders are being served. To satisfy this duty, the directors take a proactive, focused approach to their position, and
set standards to ensure that the Company is committed to business success through maintenance of high standards of responsibility and ethics. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="2">Members of the Board bring to the Company a wide range of experience and knowledge, and bring these skills to bear for the Company. These varied skills mean that good governance depends on far more than a &#147;check the box&#148; approach
to standards or procedures. The governance structure in the Company is designed to be a working structure for principled actions, effective decision-making and appropriate monitoring of both compliance and performance. The key practices and
procedures of the Board are outlined in the Corporate Governance Guidelines available on the Company&#146;s website at www.apple.com/investor. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="2">The Board met a total of five times during fiscal 2008. The Board has determined that all Board members, excluding Mr.&nbsp;Jobs, are independent under the applicable NASDAQ and SEC rules. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Board Committees </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Board has a standing Audit and

</TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Audit Committee is responsible primarily for overseeing the services performed by the
Company&#146;s independent registered public accounting firm and internal audit department, evaluating the Company&#146;s accounting policies and system of internal controls and reviewing significant financial transactions. The Audit Committee met a
total of eleven times during fiscal 2008. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Compensation Committee is responsible primarily for reviewing the compensation arrangements
for the Company&#146;s executive officers, including the CEO, and for administering the Company&#146;s equity compensation plans. The Compensation Committee&#146;s authority may not be delegated to the Company&#146;s management or others. The
Compensation Committee met a total of four times during fiscal 2008. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">9 </FONT></P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" COLOR="#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Nominating Committee assists the Board in identifying qualified individuals to become directors,
determines the composition of the Board and its committees, monitors the process to assess the Board&#146;s effectiveness and helps develop and implement the Company&#146;s Corporate Governance Guidelines. The Nominating Committee also considers
nominees for election as directors proposed by shareholders. The Nominating Committee is committed to actively seeking out highly qualified women and individuals from minority groups to include in the pool from which Board nominees are chosen. The
Nominating Committee met a total of five times during fiscal 2008 and met after the end of the last fiscal year to recommend to the full Board each of the nominees for election to the Board, as presented herein. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Audit Committee, Compensation Committee and Nominating Committee operate under written charters adopted by the Board. These charters are available on
the Company&#146;s website at www.apple.com/investor. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">During fiscal 2008, each member of the Board attended or participated in 75% or more
of the aggregate of (i)&nbsp;the total number of meetings of the Board (held during the period for which such person has been a director) and (ii)&nbsp;the total number of meetings held by all committees of the Board on which such person served
(during the periods that such person served). </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">There are no family relationships among executive officers and directors of the Company.
</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Audit Committee Financial Experts </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The
Board has determined that all members of the Audit Committee, Messrs. Campbell and York and Dr.&nbsp;Levinson, qualify as &#147;audit committee financial experts&#148; as defined by the SEC and also meet the additional criteria for independence of
audit committee members set forth in Rule 10A-3(b)(l) under the Exchange Act. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Code of Ethics </B></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Company has a code of ethics, &#147;Business Conduct: The Way We Do Business Worldwide,&#148; that applies to all of the Company&#146;s employees,
including its principal executive officer, principal financial officer and principal accounting officer, and the Board. A copy of this code is available on the Company&#146;s website at www.apple.com/investor. The Company intends to disclose any
changes in or waivers from its code of ethics by posting such information on its website or by filing a Form 8-K. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Compensation of Directors
</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The form and amount of director compensation are determined by the Board after its review of recommendations made by the Nominating
Committee. The current practice of the Board is to base a substantial portion of a director&#146;s annual retainer on equity. Under the Company&#146;s 1997 Director Stock Option Plan (the &#147;<I>Director Plan</I>&#148;), members of the Board who
are not also Company employees (&#147;<I>Non-Employee Directors</I>&#148;) are granted an option to acquire 30,000 shares of the Company&#146;s common stock upon their initial election or appointment to the Board (an &#147;<I>Initial
Option</I>&#148;). Initial Options vest and become exercisable in equal installments on each of the first three anniversaries of the grant date. Starting on the fourth anniversary of a Non-Employee Director&#146;s initial election or appointment to
the Board and on each subsequent anniversary thereafter during the director&#146;s tenure on the Board, the Non-Employee Director is granted an option to acquire 10,000 shares of the Company&#146;s common stock (an &#147;<I>Annual Option</I>&#148;).
Annual Options are fully vested and immediately exercisable on the date of grant. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Non-Employee Directors also receive a $50,000 annual
retainer paid in quarterly installments, and the Chair of the Audit Committee receives an additional annual retainer of $25,000. In addition, under the Company&#146;s Board of Directors Equipment Program, each Non-Employee Director is eligible to
receive, upon request and free of charge, one of each new product introduced by the Company and is eligible to purchase additional equipment at a discount. In 2008, each Non-Employee Director was offered a commemorative gift for Board </FONT>
</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">10 </FONT></P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" COLOR="#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">
<FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">service and a payment to cover the tax liability to the director arising from the gift and the payment itself. Other than the Chair of the Audit Committee,
directors do not receive any additional compensation for serving as a Chair or member of any other committee. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Since his initial
appointment to the Board on August&nbsp;29, 2006, Dr.&nbsp;Schmidt has declined the annual retainer fee and declined to participate in the Director Plan, under which he would have received an Initial Option to acquire 30,000 shares of the
Company&#146;s common stock. In September 2006, Dr.&nbsp;Schmidt purchased 10,000 shares of the Company&#146;s common stock on the open market. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"

director or a member of a compensation committee (or other committee serving an equivalent function) of any other entity, the executive officers of which served as a director of the Company or member of the Compensation Committee during fiscal 2008.

</TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Timothy D. Cook</B>, Chief Operating Officer, joined the Company in March 1998. Mr.&nbsp;Cook
also served as Executive Vice President, Worldwide Sales and Operations from 2002 to 2005. In 2004, his responsibilities were expanded to include the Company&#146;s Macintosh hardware engineering. From 2000 to 2002, Mr.&nbsp;Cook served as Senior
Vice President, Worldwide Operations, Sales, Service and Support. From 1998 to 2000, Mr.&nbsp;Cook served as Senior Vice President, Worldwide Operations. Prior to joining the Company, Mr.&nbsp;Cook was Vice President, Corporate Materials for Compaq
Computer Corporation (&#147;<I>Compaq</I>&#148;). Prior to his work at Compaq, Mr.&nbsp;Cook was Chief Operating Officer of the Reseller Division at Intelligent Electronics. Mr.&nbsp;Cook also spent 12 years with IBM, most recently as Director of
North American Fulfillment. Mr.&nbsp;Cook also serves as a member of the Board of Directors of Nike, Inc. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Daniel Cooperman</B>, Senior
Vice President, General Counsel and Secretary, joined the Company in November 2007. Prior to joining the Company, he served as Senior Vice President, General Counsel and Secretary of Oracle Corporation since February 1997. Prior to that, he had been
associated with the law firm of McCutchen, Doyle, Brown&nbsp;&amp; Enersen (which is now Bingham McCutchen LLP) since October 1977 and had served as a partner since June 1983. From September 1995 until February 1997, Mr.&nbsp;Cooperman was Chair of
the law firm&#146;s Business and Transactions Group, and from April 1989 through September 1995 he served as Managing Partner of the law firm&#146;s San Jose office. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Scott Forstall</B>, Senior Vice President, iPhone Software Engineering and Platform Experience, joined the Company in February 1997 upon the Company&#146;s acquisition of NeXT. Mr.&nbsp;Forstall also has served the
Company as Vice President of Platform Experience while leading several releases of Mac OS X, and as Director of Application Frameworks. Prior to joining the Company, Mr.&nbsp;Forstall worked at NeXT developing core technologies. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Ronald B. Johnson</B>,<B> </B>Senior Vice President, Retail, joined the Company in January 2000. Prior to joining the Company, Mr.&nbsp;Johnson spent
16 years with Target Stores, most recently as Senior Merchandising Executive. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Robert Mansfield</B>,<B></B> Senior Vice President, Mac
Hardware Engineering, joined the Company in November 1999 as Vice President of Development Engineering and assumed his current position in May 2008. Prior to joining the Company, Mr.&nbsp;Mansfield was Vice President of Engineering at Raycer
Graphics and a Senior Director at Silicon Graphics, Inc. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Peter Oppenheimer</B>, Senior Vice President and Chief Financial Officer, joined the Company in July
1996. Mr.&nbsp;Oppenheimer also served the Company as Vice President and Corporate Controller and as Senior Director of Finance for the Americas. Prior to joining the Company, Mr.&nbsp;Oppenheimer was Chief Financial Officer of one of the four
business units for Automatic Data Processing, Inc. (&#147;<I>ADP</I>&#148;). Prior to joining ADP, Mr.&nbsp;Oppenheimer spent six years in the Information Technology Consulting Practice with Coopers and Lybrand. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Philip W. Schiller</B>, Senior Vice President, Worldwide Product Marketing, rejoined the Company in 1997. Prior to rejoining the Company,
Mr.&nbsp;Schiller was Vice President of Product Marketing at Macromedia, Inc. from December 1995 to March 1997 and Director of Product Marketing at FirePower Systems, Inc. from 1993 to December 1995. Prior to that, Mr.&nbsp;Schiller spent six years
at the Company in various marketing positions. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Bertrand Serlet</B>, Senior Vice President, Software Engineering, joined the Company in
February 1997 upon the Company&#146;s acquisition of NeXT and also served the Company as Vice President of Platform Technology. At NeXT, Mr.&nbsp;Serlet held several engineering and managerial positions, including Director of Web Engineering. Prior
to NeXT, Mr.&nbsp;Serlet worked as a research engineer at Xerox PARC from 1985 to 1989. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Sina Tamaddon</B>, Senior Vice President,
Applications, joined the Company in September 1997. Mr.&nbsp;Tamaddon has also served with the Company as Senior Vice President, Worldwide Service and Support, and Vice President and General Manager, Newton Group. Before joining the Company,
Mr.&nbsp;Tamaddon held the position of Vice President, Europe with NeXT from September 1996 through March 1997. From August 1994 to August 1996, Mr.&nbsp;Tamaddon was Vice President, Professional Services with NeXT. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>

STYLE="margin-top:24px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>SECTION&nbsp;16(a) BENEFICIAL OWNERSHIP REPORTING COMPLIANCE </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Section&nbsp;16(a) of the Exchange Act requires the Company&#146;s officers and directors, and persons who own more than ten percent of a registered class of the Company&#146;s equity securities, to file reports of
securities ownership and changes in such ownership with the SEC. Officers, directors and greater than ten percent shareholders also are required by rules promulgated by the SEC to furnish the Company with copies of all Section&nbsp;16(a) forms they
file. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Based solely upon a review of the copies of such forms furnished to the Company or written representations that no Forms 5 were
required, the Company believes that all Section&nbsp;16(a) filing requirements were met during fiscal 2008. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:24px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>REVIEW, APPROVAL OR
RATIFICATION OF TRANSACTIONS WITH RELATED PERSONS </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Board has adopted a written policy for approval of transactions between the
Company and its directors, director nominees, executive officers, greater than five percent beneficial owners and their respective immediate family members, where the amount involved in the transaction exceeds or is expected to exceed $120,000 in a
single calendar year. A copy of this policy is available on the Company&#146;s website at www.apple.com/investor. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The policy provides that
the Audit Committee reviews transactions subject to the policy and determines whether or not to approve or ratify those transactions. In doing so, the Audit Committee takes into account, among other factors it deems appropriate: </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="5%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">the related person&#146;s interest in the transaction; </FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">17 </FONT></P>

<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="5%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">the approximate dollar value of the amount involved in the transaction; </FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P
STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="5%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">the approximate dollar value of the amount of the related person&#146;s interest in the transaction without regard to the amount of any profit or loss;
</FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="5%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>

<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">whether the transaction was undertaken in the ordinary course of business of the Company; </FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P
STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>

reached with an unrelated third party; </FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">any other information regarding the transaction or the related person in the context of the proposed transaction that would be material to investors in light of the
circumstances of the particular transaction. </FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">In addition, the Audit Committee has delegated authority to the Chair of

</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Audit Committee has considered and adopted standing pre-approvals under the policy for limited transactions with related persons.

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>EXECUTIVE COMPENSATION </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B><I>Compensation Committee Report </I></B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>The following report of the Compensation Committee shall not
be deemed to be &#147;soliciting material&#148; or to otherwise be considered &#147;filed&#148; with the SEC, nor shall such information be incorporated by reference into any future filing under the Securities Act of 1933 (the &#147;Securities
Act&#148;) or the Exchange Act except to the extent that the Company specifically incorporates it by reference into such filing. </I></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The
Compensation Committee consists of three Non-Employee Directors: Messrs. Campbell, Drexler and Gore, each of whom the Board has determined is independent under the applicable NASDAQ and SEC rules. The Compensation Committee has certain duties and
powers as described in its written charter adopted by the Board. A copy of the charter can be found on the Company&#146;s website at www.apple.com/investor. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Compensation Committee has reviewed and discussed with management the disclosures contained in the section entitled &#147;Compensation Discussion and Analysis&#148; of this Proxy Statement. Based upon this review
and discussion, the Compensation Committee recommended to the Board that the section entitled &#147;Compensation Discussion and Analysis&#148; be included in this Proxy Statement for the Annual Meeting. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:24px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Members of the Compensation Committee </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>

</TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B><I>Compensation Discussion and Analysis </I></B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>A. Executive Summary </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">This section explains the Company&#146;s executive compensation program as it
relates to the following &#147;named executive officers&#148; whose compensation information is presented in the tables following this discussion in accordance with SEC rules: </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>

</TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">In fiscal 2008, each named executive officer was a member of the Company&#146;s executive team,
the Company&#146;s most senior management committee. On November&nbsp;3, 2008, Mr.&nbsp;Fadell became Special Advisor to the Chief Executive Officer, as discussed in the section entitled &#147;F. Fiscal 2009 Compensation Decisions&#151;3. Tony
Fadell Agreement&#148; below. In this new position, Mr.&nbsp;Fadell is no longer an executive officer of the Company. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Company&#146;s
executive compensation program for the named executive officers, other than Mr.&nbsp;Jobs, consists of long-term equity awards in the form of RSUs and cash compensation in the form of performance-based cash incentives and base salaries. In fiscal
2008, Mr.&nbsp;Jobs&#146; entire compensation consisted of a base salary of $1. Each year, the Compensation Committee determines the compensation for the named executive officers. The Compensation Committee believes the Company&#146;s compensation
strategy has served the Company well. As a result, no significant changes were made to the Company&#146;s executive compensation program in fiscal 2008. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Company continues to rely on long-term equity awards in the form of RSUs to attract and retain an outstanding executive team and to ensure a strong connection between executive compensation and financial </FONT>
</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">20 </FONT></P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" COLOR="#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">
<FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">performance. The Compensation Committee annually reviews the outstanding, unvested equity awards of each named executive officer to determine whether
additional awards are warranted in light of the officer&#146;s performance, the competitive environment and the other factors discussed in the section entitled &#147;D. Executive Compensation Program Design and Implementation&#151;3. The Role of
Long-Term Equity Awards&#148; below. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The performance-based cash incentives are designed to compensate the named executive officers for
achieving specific financial goals established annually by the Compensation Committee, as described in the section entitled &#147;D. Executive Compensation Program Design and Implementation&#151;4. The Role of Cash Compensation&#148; below. The
Compensation Committee sets aggressive performance goals each year based on the revenue and operating income objectives in the Company&#146;s internal business plan. Payments are not automatic even if the goals are achieved, however, because the
Compensation Committee may exercise its discretion to reduce (but not increase) the amount of any incentive payment based on an officer&#146;s overall performance. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Compensation Committee believes the compensation program for the named executive officers has been instrumental in helping the Company achieve its business objectives and is appropriate and fair in light of the
Company&#146;s strong financial performance relative to that of its peer group. In fiscal 2008, the Company&#146;s revenue grew to $32.5 billion, representing an increase of $8.5 billion or 35% over the prior year. Net income also increased
markedly, growing to $4.8 billion in fiscal 2008, an increase of $1.3 billion or 38% over the prior year. The Company&#146;s strong earnings and operational excellence in fiscal 2008 helped drive an ending cash balance of $24.5 billion, representing
growth of $9.1 billion or 59% over the prior year. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>B. Executive Compensation Objectives </B></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Company&#146;s goal for executive compensation is to attract and retain a talented, entrepreneurial and creative team of executives who will provide
the leadership for the Company&#146;s success in dynamic, competitive markets. The Compensation Committee seeks to accomplish this goal while ensuring that the executive compensation program is aligned with the long-term interests of the
Company&#146;s shareholders. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>C. Executive Compensation Overview </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:2%"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B><I>1. Three Components </I></B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The compensation program for the named executive officers, other than
Mr.&nbsp;Jobs, consists of the following three components, in order of their importance: </FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="5%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">long-term equity awards in the form of RSUs under the shareholder-approved 2003 Employee Stock Plan; </FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P
STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="5%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">annual performance-based cash incentives under the shareholder-approved Performance Bonus Plan; and </FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P
STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="5%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">base salary. </FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The named executive officers are also
eligible to participate in the Company&#146;s health and welfare programs, Employee Stock Purchase Plan, 401(k) Plan, patent bonus program and other employee recognition programs on the same basis as other employees. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:2%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B><I>2. Mix of Equity, Cash Incentives and Salary </I></B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Company relies on long-term equity awards in the form of RSUs because the Company and the Compensation Committee believe they are the most effective compensation element for attracting entrepreneurial, creative
executives and promoting their long-term commitment to the Company. An RSU award generally vests only if the named executive officer continues employment until the specified vesting date. To help promote retention, the Compensation Committee has
established vesting intervals of no less than two years </FONT>
</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">21 </FONT></P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" COLOR="#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">
<FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">for ongoing RSU awards for the named executive officers. RSU awards also help to ensure a strong connection between executive compensation and the interests
of the Company&#146;s shareholders because the value of RSUs depends on the Company&#146;s future share price. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Although the Compensation
Committee reviews the compensation practices of its peer companies as described in the section entitled &#147;D. Executive Compensation Program Design and Implementation&#151;6. The Role of Peer Groups, Surveys and Benchmarking&#148; below, the
Compensation Committee does not adhere to strict formulas or rely to any significant extent on survey data to determine the mix of compensation elements. Instead, as described in the section entitled &#147;D. Executive Compensation Program Design
and Implementation&#148; below, the Compensation Committee considers a variety of factors in exercising its discretion to determine compensation, including the experience, responsibilities and performance of each named executive officer and the
Company&#146;s overall financial performance. This flexibility is particularly important in designing compensation arrangements to attract new executives in the highly-competitive, rapidly changing market in which the Company competes. </FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:2%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B><I>3. Elements of Compensation Not Included in the Compensation Program </I></B></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The current compensation program for the named executive officers, including Mr.&nbsp;Jobs, generally does <I>not</I> include the following: </FONT></P>
<P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>

STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>

<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">guarantees of the value of equity awards. </FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:2%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="2"><B><I>4. CEO Compensation </I></B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Mr.&nbsp;Jobs currently holds approximately 5.5&nbsp;million shares of the Company&#146;s common
stock. Since rejoining the Company in 1997, Mr.&nbsp;Jobs has never sold a share of the Company&#146;s stock. Mr.&nbsp;Jobs currently holds no unvested equity awards. In fiscal 2008, Mr.&nbsp;Jobs&#146; compensation consisted of his $1 annual
salary. The Compensation Committee recognizes that Mr.&nbsp;Jobs&#146; level of stock ownership significantly aligns his interests with those of the Company&#146;s shareholders. Nevertheless, because Mr.&nbsp;Jobs&#146; continued leadership is
critical to the Company, the Compensation Committee from time to time considers additional compensation arrangements for him. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>D. Executive Compensation
Program Design and Implementation </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:2%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B><I>1. Team-Based Compensation </I></B></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The compensation program for the named executive officers rests on two assumptions. First, each officer must demonstrate exceptional personal performance
in order to remain part of the executive team. Second, each officer must contribute as a member of the team to the Company&#146;s overall success rather than merely achieve specific objectives within that officer&#146;s area of responsibility.
Because of this team-based approach to compensation, the Compensation Committee carefully considers the relative compensation levels among all members of the executive team. Accordingly, the Company&#146;s executive compensation program is designed
to be internally consistent and equitable in order to further the Company&#146;s success and achieve its executive compensation objectives. The reasons for differences in the amounts awarded to each of the named executive officers relate primarily
to the experience, responsibilities and performance of each named executive officer. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">22 </FONT></P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" COLOR="#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:2%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B><I>2. Independent Compensation Committee Determines All Executive Compensation </I></B></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Compensation Committee determines all compensation for the named executive officers. All three Compensation Committee members are independent
directors under the applicable NASDAQ and SEC rules. Each fiscal year, the Compensation Committee conducts an evaluation of each named executive officer to determine if changes in the officer&#146;s compensation are appropriate based on the
considerations described below. Mr.&nbsp;Jobs does not participate in the Compensation Committee&#146;s deliberations or decisions with regard to his compensation. At the Compensation Committee&#146;s request, Mr.&nbsp;Jobs reviews with the
Compensation Committee the performance of the other named executive officers. The Compensation Committee gives considerable weight to Mr.&nbsp;Jobs&#146; evaluation of the other named executive officers because of his direct knowledge of each
officer&#146;s performance and contributions. No other named executive officer has any input into executive compensation decisions. For each officer, the Compensation Committee members independently determine each component of compensation based on
their collective assessment of the officer&#146;s performance as well as the Company&#146;s overall financial performance. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:2%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B><I>3. The
Role of Long-Term Equity Awards </I></B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>Overview</I>. The Compensation Committee believes that long-term equity awards are the most
effective way to attract and retain an executive team. Accordingly, executive compensation is weighted toward long-term equity awards rather than cash compensation, and the awards have long vesting intervals to maximize their retention value.
Because of the emphasis on RSU awards with long vesting intervals, the executive team&#146;s compensation also is closely aligned with the long-term interests of the Company&#146;s shareholders. This approach is reflected in the following:
</FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="5%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">equity awards for the named executive officers, other than Mr.&nbsp;Jobs, represented approximately 85% of their target total compensation in fiscal 2008. This
compares to approximately 70% at the Company&#146;s peer companies; </FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="5%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">fiscal 2004 equity awards vested 50% in 2006; the remaining 50% vested in 2008; </FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P
STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="5%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>

<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">fiscal 2006 equity awards do not vest at all until 2010, when they vest in full; and </FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P
STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="5%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">fiscal 2008 equity awards do not vest at all until 2012, when they vest in full. </FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">In designing long-term equity awards, the Compensation Committee seeks to maximize their effectiveness in accomplishing the Company&#146;s compensation objectives while recognizing the Board&#146;s duty to the
Company&#146;s shareholders to limit equity dilution. The Compensation Committee believes this balance has been achieved as follows: </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="2"><I>Restricted Stock Units Minimize Dilution</I>. Since fiscal 2004, all of the Company&#146;s equity awards to its named executive officers have been RSUs rather than stock options. A grant of RSUs gives an officer the right to receive a
specified number of shares of the Company&#146;s common stock, at no cost to the officer, if the officer remains employed at the Company until the RSUs vest. Although its value may increase or decrease with changes in the stock price during the
period between granting and vesting, an RSU will have value in the long term. By contrast, the entire compensation value of a stock option depends on future stock price appreciation. Accordingly, RSUs can deliver significantly greater
share-for-share compensation value at grant than stock options, and the Company can offer comparable grant date compensation value with fewer shares and less dilution for its shareholders. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>Long Vesting Intervals Maximize Retention and Support Long-Term Focus</I>. Vesting of RSUs is subject to continued employment. RSUs provide for
partial accelerated vesting only upon death or disability of the officer. Except for occasional new hire grants, promotion grants, and retention grants, vesting occurs at intervals of no less than two years after the grant date. This helps ensure
that a meaningful portion of a named executive officer&#146;s awards will vest every two years, which is intended to retain the named executive officers and cause them to focus on the Company&#146;s long-term business objectives. The following table
shows the grant and vesting </FONT>
</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">23 </FONT></P>

<HR  SIZE="3" COLOR="#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">
<FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">patterns for ongoing RSU grants for the named executive officers since fiscal 2004 (excluding those grants to individuals who were not named executive
officers at the time of grant). </FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>

</TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>Reduction in Annual Burn Rate to 2.16%</I>. In fiscal 2005, the Company committed to an annual
&#147;burn rate&#148; (which is generally defined as the total number of shares subject to all equity awards granted during the fiscal year divided by the total number of shares outstanding at the end of the fiscal year) of 2.5% from fiscal 2005
through fiscal 2007. This commitment represented a significant reduction from an annual average burn rate of 4.8% from fiscal 2002 through fiscal 2004. The Company met this commitment from fiscal 2005 through fiscal 2007 and continued to meet this
commitment in fiscal 2008. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>Reduction in Overhang from Equity Plans to 10.8%</I>. Overhang (which is generally defined as the number of
shares subject to granted and outstanding equity awards plus the number of shares reserved for future awards, divided by the sum of total shares outstanding, granted and outstanding equity awards, and shares reserved for future awards) is another
measure of equity dilution. The efficient use of equity awards, combined with the exercise of a substantial number of employee stock options due to the significant increase in the Company&#146;s stock price over the past few years, has caused the
Company&#146;s overhang to decline from approximately 14.5% at the end of fiscal 2005 to approximately 10.8% at the end of fiscal 2008. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="2"><I>Frequency and Size of RSU Awards</I>. The named executive officers typically receive RSU awards approximately every two years, rather than every year. This practice is consistent with the long time horizon and lengthy vesting periods of
the awards. By making awards less frequently, the Compensation Committee can provide larger grants, which in turn promotes greater retention. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="2">To determine the size of RSU grants, the Compensation Committee first establishes a target compensation value to be delivered to the named executive officers through long-term equity awards. In doing so, the Compensation Committee considers
various factors, including the following: </FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="5%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">the practice of granting ongoing equity awards only approximately every two years; </FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P
STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="5%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">the emphasis placed on equity in the mix of total compensation; </FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>

<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">the officer&#146;s experience and performance; </FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="5%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">the scope, responsibility and business impact of the officer&#146;s position; and </FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P
STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="5%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="2%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#149;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">the perceived retention value of the total compensation package in light of the competitive labor market. </FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P
STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Once the target value has been established, the Compensation Committee determines the number of shares to be subject to the awards by reference to the current value of
the Company&#146;s common stock. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:2%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B><I>4. The Role of Cash Compensation </I></B></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>Base Salaries</I>. The Compensation Committee believes that base salaries are less important than performance-based bonuses and long-term equity awards
in meeting the Company&#146;s compensation objectives. The de-emphasized role of salaries as part of total compensation is reflected in the following: </FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">

<TD WIDTH="1%" VALIGN="top"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Mr.&nbsp;Jobs has received an annual base salary of $1 since rejoining the Company in 1997; </FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">base salaries for the named executive officers have not increased since October 2005, except for a promotion-related increase for Mr.&nbsp;Fadell in 2006 and annual
increases for Mr.&nbsp;Mansfield before he became a member of the executive team. </FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>Performance-Based Cash
Incentives</I>. The Performance Bonus Plan, which has been approved by the Company&#146;s shareholders, authorizes the Compensation Committee to issue plan-based cash incentive awards to compensate officers for achieving specific financial
objectives that are established annually. The Compensation Committee believes that performance-based cash compensation is an important component of executive compensation because it rewards the named executive officers for achieving the short-term
performance goals established by the Company; however, it represents a small percentage of the executives&#146; total compensation because the Compensation Committee believes that cash bonus programs are less effective in attracting new executive
talent than equity compensation, and promote retention only in the short-term&#151;over the performance period. Accordingly, the plan is modestly funded, as reflected by the following: </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>

450% of base salary) is becoming increasingly common. </FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Compensation Committee establishes performance goals each year
based on revenue and operating income objectives in the Company&#146;s internal business plan. The Compensation Committee has selected these performance goals because they are indicators of increased shareholder value. These performance goals
generally exclude the effects of extraordinary, unusual or infrequently occurring events or changes in accounting principles. Because the business plan is highly confidential, the Company does not publicly disclose specific annual internal revenue
or operating income objectives. Revealing specific objectives would provide competitors and other third parties with insights into the Company&#146;s confidential planning process and strategies, thereby causing competitive harm. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Compensation Committee next determines the maximum amount of any cash incentive payment denominated as a percentage of the executive&#146;s base

</TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The performance goals are designed to be aggressive, and there is a risk that payments will not be
made at all or will be made at less than 100% of the target amount (i.e., 50% of the executive&#146;s base salary). For the past four years, the performance goals have reflected double-digit growth in both revenue and operating income. In four of
the past nine years, the Company did not meet one or both performance goals. This uncertainty helps ensure that any payments under the plan are truly performance-based, consistent with the plan&#146;s objectives. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">25 </FONT></P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" COLOR="#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">At the end of the year, the Compensation Committee determines the amount of the award to be paid to each
officer by comparing actual results to the performance goals. The Compensation Committee may, in its discretion, reduce (but not increase) the amount of any individual award based on the officer&#146;s overall performance. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Based on the factors discussed in the section entitled &#147;F. Fiscal 2009 Compensation Decisions&#151;2. Criteria for Performance-Based Cash
Incentives&#148; below, the Compensation Committee determined that it would be more effective to change the performance criteria used for the performance-based cash incentive program from revenue and operating income to adjusted sales and adjusted
operating income in fiscal 2009. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:2%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B><I>5. The Role of Consultants </I></B></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Compensation Committee has selected and directly retains the services of Frederic&nbsp;W. Cook&nbsp;&amp; Co.,&nbsp;Inc. (&#147;<I>F.W.
Cook</I>&#148;), an independent executive compensation consulting firm. F.W.&nbsp;Cook only provides compensation consulting services on matters for which the Compensation Committee is responsible. F.W. Cook does not perform other work for the
Company. The Compensation Committee periodically seeks input from F.W.&nbsp;Cook on a range of external market factors, including evolving compensation trends, appropriate comparison companies and market survey data. F.W.&nbsp;Cook also provides
general observations on the Company&#146;s compensation programs, but it does not determine or recommend the amount or form of compensation for any executives. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:2%"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B><I>6. The Role of Peer Groups, Surveys and Benchmarking </I></B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">With the assistance of F.W. Cook, the
Compensation Committee identified peer companies for fiscal 2008 that compete with the Company in the labor and capital markets and that follow similar pay models. Adjustments are made to the peer group each year based on a comparison of market
capitalization, industry and company performance. The peer companies for fiscal 2008 are as follows: </FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
