compensation practices at peer companies (gathered from SEC filings and the Radford High Technology compensation survey) to help ensure that the Company&#146;s total compensation is within a reasonably competitive range. The Compensation Committee,
however, does not set compensation components to meet specific benchmarks, such as targeting salaries &#147;above the median&#148; or equity compensation &#147;at the 75</FONT><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1"><SUP>th</SUP></FONT><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"> percentile.&#148; Furthermore, the Compensation Committee believes that over-reliance on benchmarking can result in compensation that is unrelated to the value delivered by the named executive officers. </FONT></P>
<P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:2%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B><I>7. Tax Considerations </I></B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="2"><I>Tax Deductibility of Compensation Expense</I>. Section&nbsp;162(m) (&#147;<I>162(m)</I>&#148;) of the Internal Revenue Code of 1986, as amended (the &#147;<I>Internal Revenue Code</I>&#148;), places a limit of $1,000,000 on the amount of
compensation to the Company&#146;s chief executive officer and the three most highly-compensated named executive officers employed by the Company at the end of the year (other than the Company&#146;s chief financial officer) that may be deducted by
the Company as a business expense in any tax year unless, among other things, the compensation is </FONT>
</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">26 </FONT></P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" COLOR="#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">
<FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">performance-based and provided under a plan that has been approved by the shareholders. To qualify as performance-based compensation, the compensation
generally must be approved by a committee that consists solely of at least two &#147;outside&#148; directors who have never been employed by the Company or its subsidiaries. Two members of the Compensation Committee, Messrs.&nbsp;Drexler and Gore,
qualify as outside directors under the Internal Revenue Service (&#147;<I>IRS</I>&#148;) definition. Although Mr.&nbsp;Campbell is an independent director under the applicable NASDAQ and SEC rules, he does not qualify as an outside director under
the IRS definition because he was an officer of the Company from 1983 to 1987 and of a subsidiary of the Company from 1987 to 1991. For this reason, he does not vote on any 162(m)-related matters. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Salaries for the named executive officers do not qualify as performance-based compensation. The Company&#146;s performance-based cash incentives,
however, are intended to be excluded from the 162(m) limit because they are paid based on predetermined goals established by the Compensation Committee pursuant to the shareholder-approved Performance Bonus Plan. The Company&#146;s stock options
also are intended to qualify as performance-based compensation under 162(m). The RSUs do not qualify as performance-based compensation for purposes of 162(m) because vesting is based on continued employment rather than specific performance goals.
</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>E. Fiscal 2008 Compensation Decisions </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:2%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="2"><B><I>1. Equity Grants </I></B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">In fiscal 2008, the Compensation Committee authorized the following equity grants for the named
executive officers based on its assessment of the factors discussed in the sections entitled &#147;D. Executive Compensation Program Design and Implementation&#151;1. Team-Based Compensation&#148; and &#147;D. Executive Compensation Program Design
and Implementation&#151;3. The Role of Long-Term Equity Awards&#148; above. At the time the equity grants were made it was not anticipated that additional awards would be provided in fiscal 2009 to the named executive officers because fiscal 2008
RSUs were intended to serve as equity compensation for two years (i.e., fiscal 2008 and fiscal 2009). </FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:2%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B><I>2. Base Salary Changes </I></B></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Mr.&nbsp;Mansfield received a base salary increase from $450,000 to $500,000 in connection with the Company&#146;s annual review process in December 2007.
This increase was based on Mr.&nbsp;Mansfield&#146;s performance and contributions in fiscal 2007 as determined by management. Mr.&nbsp;Mansfield received this increase prior to the time he became a member of the executive team. Based on a review of
competitive practices and the Compensation Committee&#146;s approach to place less emphasis on cash compensation, the Compensation Committee concluded that the total compensation for the other named executive officers was appropriate for fiscal 2008
without increases in salaries. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:2%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B><I>3. Performance-Based Cash Incentive Plan Payments </I></B></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Company&#146;s fiscal 2008 performance exceeded the revenue and operating income goals established under the cash incentive plan; as a result, the
named executive officers earned payouts at the maximum of 100% of base salary, pursuant to the Percentage of Salary Payable As Performance-Based Cash Incentives chart in the section entitled &#147;D. Executive Compensation Program Design and
Implementation&#151;4. The Role of Cash Compensation&#148; above. The specific payment amounts are shown in the table entitled &#147;Summary Compensation Table&#151;Fiscal 2008 and Fiscal 2007&#148; below. As noted above, Mr.&nbsp;Jobs does not
participate in the Performance Bonus Plan. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Mr.&nbsp;Mansfield was promoted to his current position of Senior Vice President, Mac Hardware
Engineering in May 2008. As a result, Mr.&nbsp;Mansfield received a pro-rated bonus under the Performance Bonus Plan based on the amount of time he served as a Senior Vice President in fiscal 2008. Prior to his promotion, Mr.&nbsp;Mansfield
participated in the FY08 Vice President and Director Quarterly Bonus Plan (the &#147;<I>Quarterly Bonus Plan</I>&#148;) and the FY08 Vice President Annual Bonus Plan (the &#147;<I>Annual Bonus Plan</I>&#148;). The Compensation Committee establishes
performance goals for the Quarterly Bonus Plan and the Annual Bonus Plan based on revenue and operating income objectives in the Company&#146;s internal business plan. Because the business plan is highly confidential, the Company does not publicly
disclose specific internal revenue or operating income objectives. Revealing specific objectives would provide competitors and other third parties with insights into the Company&#146;s confidential planning process and strategies, thereby causing
competitive harm. Mr.&nbsp;Mansfield&#146;s target bonus and maximum bonus opportunities under the Quarterly Bonus Plan were 35% and 50% of base salary, respectively, and his target bonus and maximum bonus opportunities under the Annual Bonus Plan
were 15% and 20% of base salary, respectively. The Company&#146;s performance exceeded the revenue and operating income goals established under the Quarterly Bonus Plan and the Annual Bonus Plan; as a result, Mr.&nbsp;Mansfield earned a payout at
the maximum amount, which was pro-rated based on the amount of time he participated in the Quarterly Bonus Plan and the Annual Bonus Plan prior to his promotion. Mr.&nbsp;Mansfield received a bonus of $151,100 under the Quarterly Bonus Plan and a
bonus of $60,440 under the Annual Bonus Plan for fiscal 2008. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>F. Fiscal 2009 Compensation Decisions </B></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:2%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B><I>1. Base Salary Adjustments </I></B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="2">Effective in fiscal 2009, the Compensation Committee determined that it was appropriate to increase the base salaries for a number of the members of the executive team, including the following named executive officers: Messrs. Oppenheimer,
Cook and Mansfield. This was the first salary adjustment for the named executive officers since October 2005 other than a promotion-related increase for Mr.&nbsp;Fadell in 2006 and annual increases for Mr.&nbsp;Mansfield before he became a member of
the executive team in May 2008. These salary adjustments primarily relate to the business impact of each officer&#146;s position in addition to individual performance factors. The Compensation Committee also considered the relative competitiveness
of the executive team&#146;s total cash compensation as compared to that of the peer companies. With the assistance of F.W. Cook, the Compensation Committee determined that the total cash compensation for certain members of the executive
team&nbsp;was below the median of the peer companies despite the Company&#146;s superior performance. In addition, as </FONT>
</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">28 </FONT></P>

</TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:2%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B><I>2. Criteria for Performance-Based Cash Incentives </I></B></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">In fiscal 2009, the Compensation Committee determined that it was appropriate to change the performance criteria used in determining the Company&#146;s
performance-based cash incentives from revenue and operating income to adjusted sales and adjusted operating income. The Company has disclosed certain adjusted non-GAAP financial measures to provide insight into operating and business trends not
readily apparent from GAAP results, as described in its report on Form 8-K filed with the SEC on October&nbsp;21, 2008. The Compensation Committee believes it is important to align the named executive officers&#146; performance-based cash payments
with these measures, as these are the measures that the Company&#146;s management uses in analyzing the business. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:2%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B><I>3. Tony Fadell
Agreement </I></B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">On November&nbsp;3, 2008, Mr.&nbsp;Fadell became Special Advisor to the Chief Executive Officer. In his new position,
Mr.&nbsp;Fadell is no longer an executive officer of the Company. Mr.&nbsp;Fadell and the Company have entered into a Transition Agreement and a Settlement Agreement and Release (together, the &#147;<I>Transition Agreement</I>&#148;), under which
Mr.&nbsp;Fadell will receive an annual salary of $300,000, and will be entitled to bonus and other health and welfare benefits generally available to other senior managers, subject to his continued employment with the Company. Under the terms of the
Transition Agreement, the Company cancelled 155,000 RSUs held by Mr.&nbsp;Fadell, which represented all of his outstanding and unvested RSUs. In connection with Mr.&nbsp;Fadell&#146;s new role, the Compensation Committee granted Mr.&nbsp;Fadell
77,500 RSUs that will vest in full on March&nbsp;24, 2010, subject to his continued employment with the Company through the vesting date and further subject to accelerated vesting if the Company terminates his employment without cause. The
Transition Agreement includes Mr.&nbsp;Fadell&#146;s release of claims against the Company and agreement not to solicit the Company&#146;s employees for one year following the termination of his employment. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>

<TR>
<TD WIDTH="3%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1">(1)</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="1">As noted above, Mr.&nbsp;Mansfield was promoted to his current position of Senior Vice President, Mac Hardware Engineering in May 2008. In this position, he participated in the
Performance Bonus Plan. Prior to his promotion, Mr.&nbsp;Mansfield served as Vice President, Hardware Engineering, and participated in the Quarterly Bonus Plan and the Annual Bonus Plan. As a result, Mr.&nbsp;Mansfield&#146;s target bonus and
maximum bonus opportunities were pro-rated based on the amount of time he served in each position during fiscal 2008. The amount reported in Column (d)&nbsp;of the table above reflects pro-rated target bonus amounts of $98,900 under the Performance
Bonus Plan and $151,100 under the Quarterly Bonus Plan and the Annual Bonus Plan. The amount reported in Column (e)&nbsp;of the table above reflects pro-rated maximum bonus amounts of $197,800 under the Performance Bonus Plan and $211,540 under the
Quarterly Bonus Plan and the Annual Bonus Plan. </FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Description of Plan-Based Awards </B></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Each of the &#147;Non-Equity Incentive Plan Awards&#148; reported in the table entitled &#147;Grants of Plan-Based Awards&#151;Fiscal 2008&#148; was
granted under the Company&#146;s Performance Bonus Plan (except with respect to Mr.&nbsp;Mansfield&#146;s bonus opportunities prior to his promotion as noted above). The material terms of these incentive awards are described under &#147;Executive
Compensation&#151;Compensation Discussion and Analysis&#148; in the section entitled &#147;D. Executive Compensation Program Design and Implementation&#151;4. The Role of Cash Compensation&#148; above. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Column (i)&nbsp;of the table above reports awards of RSUs granted to the named executive officers in fiscal 2008. Each of these awards was granted under,
and is subject to, the terms of the Company&#146;s 2003 Employee Stock Plan (the &#147;<I>2003 Plan</I>&#148;). The 2003 Plan is administered by the Compensation Committee. The Compensation Committee has authority to interpret the plan provisions
and make all required determinations under the plan. This authority includes making required proportionate adjustments to outstanding awards upon the occurrence of certain corporate events such as reorganizations, mergers and stock splits, and
making provision to ensure that any tax withholding obligations incurred in respect of awards are satisfied. Awards granted under the plan are generally only transferable to a beneficiary of a named executive officer upon such officer&#146;s death.
However, the Compensation Committee may establish procedures for the transfer of awards to other persons or entities, provided that such transfers comply with applicable securities laws and, with limited exceptions set forth in the plan document,
are not made for value. Under the terms of the 2003 Plan, each named executive officer&#146;s outstanding awards granted under the plan will generally terminate if the Company undergoes a corporate transaction, unless the Compensation Committee
provides for the substitution, assumption, exchange or other continuation of the outstanding awards. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Each RSU represents a contractual
right to receive one share of the Company&#146;s common stock. Awards of RSUs granted to the named executive officers for fiscal 2008 are scheduled to vest in full on March&nbsp;24, 2012, except that the awards granted to Messrs. Fadell and
Mansfield in December 2007 and the award granted to Mr.&nbsp;Mansfield in May 2008 are scheduled to vest in full on March&nbsp;24, 2010. In each case, vesting is contingent on the officer&#146;s continued employment with the Company through the
vesting date. The named executive officer does not have the right to vote or dispose of the RSUs, nor the right to receive dividends in respect of the stock units. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT
SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Potential Payments Upon Termination or Change in Control </B></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">As noted above, the Company does not have employment agreements with any of its named executive officers (except for the Transition Agreement with
Mr.&nbsp;Fadell), and the Company does not maintain any other plans or arrangements that provide for any named executive officer to receive cash severance or other cash payments in connection with a termination of such officer&#146;s employment with
the Company and/or a change in control of the Company. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Effective for grants made after April&nbsp;9, 2007, the 2003 Plan was amended to
eliminate accelerated vesting of outstanding awards in connection with a change in control of the Company. With respect to awards granted under the 2003 Plan prior to that date, such awards, to the extent then outstanding and unvested, will
generally become fully vested and, in the case of options, exercisable upon a change in control of the Company, unless the Compensation Committee provides for the substitution, assumption, exchange or other continuation of such awards. Any options
that become vested in connection with a change in control generally must be exercised prior to the change in control, or they will be canceled in exchange for the right to receive a cash payment in connection with the change in control transaction.
</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The following table lists the named executive officers and the estimated amounts they would have become entitled to under the terms of
stock options and RSU awards granted to them under the 2003 Plan prior to April&nbsp;9, 2007 had a change of control of the Company occurred on September&nbsp;27, 2008, unless the Compensation Committee had provided for the substitution, assumption,
exchange or other continuation of such awards. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>

2005 count against the shares available for grant under the 2003 Plan as two shares for every share granted. </FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>
<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="4%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">(3)</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">This number includes shares issued under the 1997 Employee Stock Option Plan (the &#147;<I>1997 Plan</I>&#148;). In August 1997, the Board approved the 1997 Plan, a non-shareholder
approved plan for grants of stock options to employees who are not officers of the Company. Based on the terms of individual option grants, options granted under the 1997 Plan generally expire 7 to 10 years after the grant date and generally become
exercisable over a period of four years, based on continued employment, with either annual or quarterly vesting. In October 2003, the Company terminated the 1997 Plan and no new options can be granted from this plan. </FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>AUDIT COMMITTEE REPORT </B></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>The following is the report of the Audit Committee with respect to the Company&#146;s audited financial statements for the fiscal year ended
September&nbsp;27, 2008. The information contained in this report shall not be deemed &#147;soliciting material&#148; or otherwise considered &#147;filed&#148; with the SEC, and such information shall not be incorporated by reference into any future
filing under the Securities Act or the Exchange Act except to the extent that the Company specifically incorporates such information by reference in such filing. </I></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Audit Committee consists of three members: Messrs. Campbell and York and Dr.&nbsp;Levinson. All of the members are independent directors under the NASDAQ and SEC audit committee structure and membership
requirements. The Audit Committee has certain duties and powers as described in its written charter adopted by the Board. A copy of the charter can be found on the Company&#146;s website at www.apple.com/investor. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Audit Committee is responsible primarily for assisting the Board in fulfilling its oversight responsibility of reviewing the financial information
that will be provided to shareholders and others, appointing the independent registered public accounting firm, reviewing the services performed by the Company&#146;s independent registered public accounting firm and internal audit department,
evaluating the Company&#146;s accounting policies and the Company&#146;s system of internal controls that management and the Board have established, and reviewing significant financial transactions. The Audit Committee does not itself prepare
financial statements or perform audits, and its members are not auditors or certifiers of the Company&#146;s financial statements. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">In
fulfilling its oversight responsibility of appointing and reviewing the services performed by the Company&#146;s independent registered public accounting firm, the Audit Committee carefully reviews the policies and procedures for the engagement of
the independent registered public accounting firm, including the scope of the audit, audit fees, auditor independence matters and the extent to which the independent registered public accounting firm may be retained to perform non-audit related
services. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Company maintains an auditor independence policy that bans its auditors from performing non-financial consulting services,
such as information technology consulting and internal audit services. This policy mandates that the Audit Committee approve the audit and non-audit services and related budget in advance, and that the Audit Committee be provided with quarterly
reporting on actual spending. This policy also mandates that the Company may not enter into auditor engagements for non-audit services without the express approval of the Audit Committee. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Audit Committee has reviewed and discussed the audited financial statements for the fiscal year ended September&nbsp;27, 2008 with the Company&#146;s
management and KPMG LLP, the Company&#146;s independent registered public accounting firm (&#147;<I>KPMG</I>&#148;). The Audit Committee has also discussed with KPMG the matters required to be discussed by Statement on Auditing Standards
No.&nbsp;61, &#147;Communication with Audit Committees.&#148; </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Audit Committee also has received and reviewed the written disclosures
and the letter from KPMG required by applicable requirements of the Public Company Accounting Oversight Board regarding KPMG&#146;s communications with the Audit Committee concerning independence, and has discussed with KPMG its independence.
</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Based on the reviews and discussions referred to above, the Audit Committee recommended to the Board that the financial statements
referred to above be included in the Annual Report. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:24px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Members of the Audit Committee </B></FONT></P> <P

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>APPOINTMENT OF INDEPENDENT REGISTERED PUBLIC ACCOUNTING FIRM </B></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">In November 2008, the Audit Committee adopted and approved a plan to review the appointment of the Company&#146;s independent registered public
accounting firm every five years, effective this year. This plan coincides with the requirement under the Sarbanes-Oxley Act of 2002 and applicable regulations that the firm&#146;s lead partner and concurring partner must rotate off the account
every five years. KPMG has served as the Company&#146;s independent registered public accounting firm since fiscal 1997. The Audit Committee has reappointed KPMG as the Company&#146;s registered independent public accounting firm and approved its
fees for fiscal 2009. As part of its current review, the Audit Committee intends to invite KPMG and other independent registered public accounting firms to be considered for the engagement to serve as the Company&#146;s independent registered public
accounting firm for the remainder of fiscal 2009. The Company therefore is not asking shareholders to ratify at the Annual Meeting the appointment of KPMG as the Company&#146;s independent registered public accounting firm for fiscal 2009.
Representatives of KPMG will be present at the Annual Meeting and will have an opportunity to respond to appropriate questions. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:24px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>FEES

information technology consulting and internal audit services. This policy mandates that the Audit Committee approve the audit and non-audit services and related budget in advance, and that the Audit Committee be provided with quarterly reporting on

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>OVERVIEW OF PROPOSALS </B></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">This Proxy Statement contains five proposals requiring shareholder action. Proposal No.&nbsp;1 requests the election of eight directors to the Board.
Proposals No.&nbsp;2, No.&nbsp;3, No.&nbsp;4 and No.&nbsp;5 are shareholder proposals. Each of the proposals is discussed in more detail in the pages that follow. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:24px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>PROPOSAL NO. 1 </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Election of Directors </B></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Board has nominated directors Campbell, Drexler, Gore, Jobs, Jung, Levinson, Schmidt and York to be elected to serve until the next annual meeting of
shareholders and until their successors are duly elected and qualified. Holders of proxies solicited by this Proxy Statement will vote the proxies received by them as directed on the proxy card or, if no direction is made, for the election of the
Board&#146;s eight nominees. If any nominee is unable or declines to serve as a director at the time of the Annual Meeting, the proxy holders will vote for a nominee designated by the present Board to fill the vacancy. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Vote Required </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The eight nominees receiving the
highest number of affirmative votes of the outstanding shares of the Company&#146;s common stock present or represented by proxy and voting at the Annual Meeting, will be elected as directors to serve until the next annual meeting of shareholders
and until their successors are duly elected and qualified. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Recommendation of the Board </B></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>The Board recommends that shareholders vote FOR the election of Messrs. Campbell, Drexler, Gore, Jobs and York, Ms.&nbsp;Jung and Drs. Levinson and
Schmidt. </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:24px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>PROPOSAL NO. 2 </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="2"><B>Shareholder Proposal Regarding Political Contributions and Expenditures Report </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Company has been advised that the
International Brotherhood of Teamsters General Fund, 25 Louisiana Avenue, NW, Washington, DC 20001, a beneficial owner of 2,659 shares of the Company&#146;s common stock, intends to submit the proposal set forth below at the Annual Meeting.
</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>RESOLVED: </B>That the shareholders of Apple Inc., (&#147;Company&#148;) hereby request that the Company provide a report, updated
semi-annually, disclosing the Company&#146;s: </FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Monetary and non-monetary political contributions and expenditures not deductible under section 162 (e)(1)(B) of the Internal Revenue Code, including but not limited to

include the following: </FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">39 </FONT></P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" COLOR="#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">


<TABLE STYLE="BORDER-COLLAPSE:COLLAPSE" BORDER="0" CELLPADDING="0" CELLSPACING="0" WIDTH="100%">
<TR>
<TD WIDTH="8%"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD WIDTH="5%" VALIGN="top" ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">c.</FONT></TD>
<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The internal guidelines or policies, if any, governing the Company&#146;s political contributions and expenditures. </FONT></TD></TR></TABLE> <P
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The report shall be presented to the Board of Directors&#146; audit committee or other relevant oversight committee and posted on the Company&#146;s
website to reduce costs to shareholders. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>SUPPORTING STATEMENT: </B>As long-term shareholders of Apple, we support policies that apply
transparency and accountability to corporate political spending. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Absent a system of accountability, Company assets can be used for policy
objectives that may be inimical to the long-term interests of Apple and its shareholders. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Based on available public records, the Center
for Political Accountability estimates that Apple has contributed at least $460,000 in corporate funds since the 2002 election cycle. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="2">However, relying on publicly available data does not provide a complete picture of the Company&#146;s political expenditures. For example, the Company&#146;s payments to trade associations used for political activities are undisclosed and
unknown. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Adoption of this proposal would bring our Company in line with a growing number of leading companies, including Hewlett-Packard,
Aetna and American Electric Power that support political disclosure and accountability and present this information on their websites. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The
Company&#146;s Board and its shareholders need complete disclosure to be able to fully evaluate the political use of corporate assets. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">We
urge your support <B>FOR</B> this critical governance reform. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>The Company&#146;s Statement in Opposition to Proposal No.&nbsp;2 </B></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Board of Directors recommends a vote AGAINST Proposal No.&nbsp;2. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">It is in the best interests of the Company and its shareholders for the Company to make strategic political contributions and expenditures from time to time that promote the Company&#146;s business objectives.
However, the Board believes that producing the report requested by Proposal No.&nbsp;2 would be an unnecessary and unproductive use of the Company&#146;s resources without a commensurate benefit, as these contributions and expenditures are already
well documented by existing disclosure requirements and internal policies, as described below. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Board is dedicated to the highest
standard of legal compliance, ethical behavior and accurate disclosure to the public. Numerous federal, state and local laws regulate the Company&#146;s political contributions and expenditures at all levels, and these laws and regulations include
extensive disclosure requirements. Information about all of the Company&#146;s political contributions is available to the public in easily accessible online databases. In addition to these laws and regulations, the Company&#146;s political
contributions and expenditures are governed by internal policies, including finance policies and the Company&#146;s Political Contributions and Expenditures Policy, which is publicly available at www.apple.com/investor. All of the Company&#146;s
employees (including those of the Company&#146;s subsidiaries), independent contractors and consultants, including those who engage in lobbying on behalf of the Company, are required to adhere to these policies. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Under the Company&#146;s Political Contributions and Expenditures Policy and internal finance policies, all corporate political contributions and
lobbying expenditures are subject to review, approval and processing by the Company&#146;s Government Affairs department, which ensures that all such contributions and expenditures comply with applicable laws and that all of the reports required
under those laws are timely made. The Government </FONT>
</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">40 </FONT></P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" COLOR="#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">
<FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Affairs department also manages the Company&#146;s various trade association memberships, which provide significant benefits to the Company and its
shareholders by giving the Company access to their business, technical and industry expertise and by advancing the Company&#146;s commercial interests. Depending on the trade association, a percentage of the membership dues may go to federal
lobbying and other political activities; that percentage (determined by the trade association) is by law included in the Company&#146;s publicly available federal lobbying disclosure report. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Further disclosure of the Company&#146;s membership dues to these associations could potentially put the Company at a disadvantage with its competitors
by revealing what are often negotiated rates of membership, and by highlighting the Company&#146;s strategies and priorities. Furthermore, disclosure would not provide the Company&#146;s shareholders with a greater understanding of the
Company&#146;s business objectives as they relate to its political contributions and expenditures and could instead risk misrepresenting the Company&#146;s political activities. For example, these associations may take positions on certain matters
which the Company does not support. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Board believes that the high level of disclosure already publicly available and the Company&#146;s
current internal policies are sufficient to provide information to the Company&#146;s shareholders and to ensure appropriate political use of corporate funds without undermining the strategic nature of how these funds are distributed. Any additional
disclosure would be unnecessary especially in light of the Company&#146;s significantly limited use of corporate funds for political contributions and expenditures as compared to the Company&#146;s annual total expenditures. Accordingly, the Board
does not believe such additional disclosure is in the best interests of the Company and its shareholders and recommends a vote against Proposal No.&nbsp;2. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="2"><B>Vote Required </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The affirmative vote of (i)&nbsp;a majority of the voting power present or represented by proxy and voting at
the Annual Meeting and (ii)&nbsp;a majority of the voting power required to constitute the quorum are required to approve Proposal No.&nbsp;2. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="2"><B>Recommendation of the Board of Directors </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>The Board recommends a vote AGAINST the Shareholder Proposal Regarding
Political Contributions and Expenditures Report. </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:24px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>PROPOSAL NO. 3 </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"
ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Shareholder Proposal Regarding Adoption of Principles for Health Care Reform </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="2">The Company has been advised that the AFL-CIO Reserve Fund, 815 Sixteenth Street, N.W., Washington, D.C. 20006, a beneficial owner of 500 shares of the Company&#146;s common stock, intends to submit the proposal set forth below at the
Annual Meeting. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Shareholder Proposal </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Supporting Statement </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Institute of Medicine, established by Congress as part of the National Academy of Sciences, issued five principles for reforming health insurance coverage in a report, <I>Insuring America&#146;s Health: Principles
and Recommendations</I> (2004). We believe principles for health care reform, such as those set forth by the Institute of Medicine, are essential if public confidence in our Company&#146;s commitment to health care coverage is to be maintained.
</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Access to affordable, comprehensive health care insurance is the most significant social policy issue in America according to polls by NBC
News/<I>The Wall Street Journal</I>, the Kaiser Foundation and <I>The New York Times</I>/CBS News. In our opinion, health care reform also is a central issue in the presidential campaign of 2008. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Many national organizations have made health care reform a priority. In 2007, representing &#147;a stark departure from past practice,&#148; the American
Cancer Society redirected its entire $15 million advertising budget &#147;to the consequences of inadequate health coverage&#148; in the United States (<I>The New York Times</I>, 8/31/07). </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">John Castellani, president of the Business Roundtable (representing 160 of the country&#146;s largest companies), has stated that 52 percent of the
Business Roundtable&#146;s members say health costs represent their biggest economic challenge. &#147;The cost of health care has put a tremendous weight on the U.S. economy,&#148; according to Castellani, &#147;The current situation is not
sustainable in a global, competitive workplace.&#148; (<I>BusinessWeek</I>, July&nbsp;3, 2007) </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The National Coalition on Health Care
(whose members include some of the largest publicly-held companies, institutional investors and labor unions) also has created principles for health insurance reform. According to the National Coalition on Health Care, implementing its principles
would save employers presently providing health insurance coverage an estimated $595-$848 billion in the first 10 years of implementation. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="2">We believe that the 45.7&nbsp;million Americans without health insurance result in higher costs to our Company, as well as all other U.S. companies that provide health insurance to their employees. Annual surcharges as high as $1,160 for
the uninsured are added to the total cost of each employee&#146;s health insurance, according to Kenneth Thorpe, a leading health economist at Emory University. Moreover, we feel that increasing health care costs further reduce shareholder value
when it leads companies to shift costs to employees, thereby reducing employee productivity, health and morale. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>The Company&#146;s Statement in
Opposition to Proposal No.&nbsp;3 </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Board of Directors recommends a vote AGAINST Proposal No.&nbsp;3. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Comprehensive health care reform is a complex legislative and public policy matter that requires vigorous discussion and debate in public forums among
members of the public and those in health care and health insurance industries with relevant knowledge and expertise. The Board believes that adoption of the broad and vague principles of one organization would not contribute constructively to this
public dialogue and may very well constrain the Company as it explores innovative solutions presented by various organizations to address the health care issues that impact the Company&#146;s employees and their families. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Company is committed to the health and well-being of its employees and their families. The Company also is aware that employee health has a direct
correlation to productivity and that providing health insurance enhances its ability to attract and retain employees. The Company continually strives to develop and implement initiatives to ensure quality, cost-effective health care coverage for
employees who meet minimum workweek requirements and to encourage healthy lifestyle changes and enhance the quality of life for all the Company&#146;s employees and their families. The following are examples of how the Company is working to improve
employee health care: </FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:12px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>

reform will require action by the U.S. Congress and the President, and input from American voters will be critical as policymakers debate the scope and cost of health care reforms. The Board does not believe that national health care reform is an
issue that should be addressed through the Company&#146;s annual meeting process. The Board believes that this proposal will not provide better health care solutions for the Company or its employees and will not benefit the Company or its
shareholders, and recommends a vote against Proposal No.&nbsp;3. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Vote Required </B></FONT></P> <P

of the voting power required to constitute the quorum are required to approve Proposal No.&nbsp;3. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Recommendation of the Board of Directors
</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>The Board recommends a vote AGAINST the Shareholder Proposal Regarding Adoption of Principles for Health Care Reform.
</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:24px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>PROPOSAL NO. 4 </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="2"><B>Shareholder Proposal Regarding Sustainability Report </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Company has been advised that As You Sow, 311 California Street,
Suite 510, San Francisco, CA 94104, on behalf of John Powers, a beneficial owner of 84 shares of the Company&#146;s common stock, intends to submit the proposal set forth below at the Annual Meeting. The proposal is co-sponsored by the Green Century
Equity Fund, 114 State Street, Suite 200, Boston, MA 02109, a beneficial owner of 7,950 shares of the Company&#146;s common stock and the New York City Office of the Comptroller, 1 Centre Street, New York, NY 10007, a beneficial owner of 2,050,097
shares of the Company&#146;s common stock. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:24px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Apple, Inc.&#151;2008 </B></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>WHEREAS:</B> Investors increasingly seek disclosure of companies&#146; social and environmental practices in the belief that they impact shareholder
value. Many investors believe companies that are good employers, environmental stewards, and corporate citizens are more likely to generate stronger financial returns, better respond to emerging issues, and enjoy long-term business success.
</FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Mainstream financial companies are also increasingly recognizing the links between sustainability performance and shareholder value.
Information from corporations on their greenhouse gas emissions and climate change policies is essential to investors as they assess the strengths of corporate securities in the context of climate change and the need for greenhouse gas emissions
reductions. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">43 </FONT></P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" COLOR="#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Globally over 2,700 companies issued reports on sustainability issues in 2007
<I>(www.corporateregister.com).</I> As such, it is no surprise that Dell, IBM, and Hewlett-Packard have taken leadership roles in these areas through the publication of comprehensive sustainability reports that address their company&#146;s impacts
with regards to greenhouse gas emissions, carbon reduction, toxics, and employee safety. In fact, these companies have provided detailed public assessments of existing emissions and made carbon reduction commitments. Apple, Inc., however, lags
behind its global industry peers on sustainability reporting, especially regarding key environmental issues such as climate change. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The
information and communication technologies sector is estimated to contribute between 2-3% of total greenhouse gas emissions. As the industry continues to develop globally, this is set to increase further. Given the industry&#146;s large social and
environmental footprint, we feel it is imperative that Apple develop clear policies and programs that address the impacts of its operations on the environment and on society. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>RESOLVED:</B> Shareholders request that the Board of Directors prepare a sustainability report describing corporate strategies regarding climate
change, specifically to reduce greenhouse gas emissions and addressing other environmental and social impacts such as toxics and recycling, as well as employee and product safety. The report, prepared at reasonable cost and omitting proprietary
information, should be published by July 2009. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>SUPPORTING STATEMENT: </B>The report should include the company&#146;s definition of
sustainability and a company-wide review of company policies, practices, and metrics related to long-term social and environmental sustainability. Taking early action to calculate emissions and prepare for standards could provide competitive
advantage, while inaction risks exposing companies to regulatory and litigation risk and reputational damage. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">We recommend that Apple use
the Global Reporting Initiative&#146;s Sustainability Reporting Guidelines (&#147;the Guidelines&#148;) to prepare the sustainability report and to use the Carbon Disclosure Project (CDP) as a means to specifically report on its greenhouse gas
emissions and reduction efforts. The Global Reporting Initiative (www.globalreporting.org) is an international organization developed with representatives from the business, environmental, human rights and labor communities. The Guidelines provide
guidance on report content, including performance on direct economic impacts, environmental, labor practices and decent work conditions, human rights, society, and product responsibility. The Guidelines provide a flexible reporting system that
allows the omission of content that is not relevant to company operations. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>The Company&#146;s Statement in Opposition to Proposal No.&nbsp;4
</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Board of Directors recommends a vote AGAINST Proposal No.&nbsp;4. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Company&#146;s commitment to increased transparency regarding its social and environmental practices is evidenced by the reports and other data
available on the Company&#146;s website, as described below. As this information already addresses many of the specific issues of interest that are described in Proposal No.&nbsp;4, the Board believes that the proposal has been substantially
addressed and publication of an additional report would produce little added value while requiring unnecessary time and expense. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The
Company recognizes its responsibility as a global citizen and continually strives to reduce the environmental impact of its operations. The Company has communicated its environmental initiatives to the Company&#146;s stakeholders and intends to
provide regular updates of the Company&#146;s efforts and accomplishments. For example, in last year&#146;s letter entitled &#147;A Greener Apple&#148; (available at www.apple.com/hotnews/agreenerapple), Mr.&nbsp;Jobs announced the unprecedented
goal of eliminating polyvinyl chloride (PVC) and brominated flame retardants (BFRs) from the Company&#146;s products by the end of 2008. This year, in the &#147;Apple 2008 Environmental Update&#148; (available at www.apple.com/environment/update),
Mr.&nbsp;Jobs has reported that all of the Company&#146;s new product designs are on track to meet the Company&#146;s 2008 year-end goal. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="2">In addition to such updates, the Company has made available a number of reports and relevant webpages. In preparing certain information in these reports and webpages, the Global Reporting Initiative (GRI) Sustainability </FONT>
</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">44 </FONT></P>

with GRI indices relating to the environment (EN), human rights (HR) and labor practices (LA) indicated where applicable: </FONT></P> <P STYLE="font-size:6px;margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">&nbsp;</P>

<TD ALIGN="left" VALIGN="top"> <P ALIGN="left"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><I>Product Environmental Reports (EN 26</I>). These reports (available at www.apple.com/environment/resources/environmentalperformance.html) have been created to
document the progress the Company has made to minimize the carbon emissions of each of the following products: MacBook Air, MacBook, MacBook Pro, iMac (20-inch), iMac (24-inch), iPhone, iPod nano and iPod touch. Each product environmental report
contains a description of the product&#146;s energy efficiency, material composition, packaging and greenhouse gas emissions. No other company in the Company&#146;s industry provides this amount of detail at the product level.

those who use such products in the workplace. </FONT></P></TD></TR></TABLE> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Board believes the various reports and webpages described above
substantially fulfill the request for information in Proposal No.&nbsp;4. In addition, the Company has already considered the GRI Guidelines when </FONT>
</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">45 </FONT></P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" COLOR="#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">
<FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">preparing certain of its reports and determined the indicators most applicable and useful in the context of the Company&#146;s business. The Board does not
believe expanding into additional areas of disclosure to prepare the sustainability report requested by Proposal No.&nbsp;4 is in the best interests of the Company&#146;s shareholders when the Company has substantially fulfilled the request for such
a report by providing the information described above. Accordingly, the Board recommends a vote against Proposal No.&nbsp;4. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Vote Required
</B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The affirmative vote of (i)&nbsp;a majority of the voting power present or represented by proxy and voting at the Annual Meeting and
(ii)&nbsp;a majority of the voting power required to constitute the quorum are required to approve Proposal No.&nbsp;4. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Recommendation of the Board of
Directors </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>The Board recommends a vote AGAINST the Shareholder Proposal Regarding Sustainability Report. </B></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:24px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>PROPOSAL NO. 5 </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Shareholder Proposal
Regarding Advisory Vote on Compensation </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Company has been advised that the AFSCME Employees Pension Plan, 1625 L Street, N.W.,
Washington, D.C. 20036, a beneficial owner of 21,318 shares of the Company&#146;s common stock, intends to submit the proposal set forth below at the Annual Meeting. The proposal is co-sponsored by The Nathan Cummings Foundation, 475 Tenth Avenue,
14th Floor, New York, NY 10018, a beneficial owner of 1,555 shares of the Company&#146;s common stock. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>RESOLVED,</B> that shareholders
of Apple Inc. (&#147;Apple&#148;) request the board of directors to adopt a policy that provides shareholders the opportunity at each annual shareholder meeting to vote on an advisory resolution, proposed by management, to ratify the compensation of
the named executive officers (&#147;NEOs&#148;) set forth in the proxy statement&#146;s Summary Compensation Table (the &#147;SCT&#148;) and the accompanying narrative disclosure of material factors provided to understand the SCT (but not the
Compensation Discussion and Analysis). The proposal submitted to shareholders should make clear that the vote is non-binding and would not affect any compensation paid or awarded to any NEO. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px; margin-left:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>SUPPORTING STATEMENT </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">In our view,
senior executive compensation at Apple has not always been structured in ways that best serve shareholders&#146; interests. For example, in 2000, Chairman and CEO Steve Jobs was given a special bonus in the form of an aircraft with a total cost of
approximately $90,000,000, out of which approximately $40.5 million was for tax reimbursement. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">We believe that existing U.S. corporate
governance arrangements, including SEC rules and share exchange listing standards, do not provide shareholders with sufficient mechanisms for providing input to boards on senior executive compensation. In contrast to U.S. practice, in the United
Kingdom, public companies allow shareholders to cast an advisory vote on the &#147;directors&#146; remuneration report,&#148; which discloses executive compensation. Such a vote isn&#146;t binding, but gives shareholders a clear voice that could
help shape senior executive compensation. A recent study of executive compensation in the U.K. before and after the adoption of the shareholder advisory vote there found that CEO cash and total compensation became more sensitive to negative
operating performance after the vote&#146;s adoption. (Sudhakar Balachandran et al., &#147;Solving the Executive Compensation Problem through Shareholder Votes? Evidence from the U.K.&#148; (Oct. 2007).) </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">46 </FONT></P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" COLOR="#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Currently U.S. share exchange listing standards require shareholder approval of equity-based compensation
plans; those plans, however, set general parameters and accord the compensation committee substantial discretion in making awards and establishing performance thresholds for a particular year. Shareholders do not have any mechanism for providing
ongoing feedback on the application of those general standards to individual pay packages. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Similarly, performance criteria submitted for
shareholder approval to allow a company to deduct compensation in excess of $1 million are broad and do not constrain compensation committees in setting performance targets for particular senior executives. Withholding votes from compensation
committee members who are standing for reelection is a blunt and insufficient instrument for registering dissatisfaction with the way in which the committee has administered compensation plans and policies in the previous year. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Accordingly, we urge Apple&#146;s board to allow shareholders to express their opinion about senior executive compensation by establishing an annual
referendum process. The results of such a vote could provide Apple with useful information about shareholders&#146; views on the company&#146;s senior executive compensation, as reported each year, and would facilitate constructive dialogue between
shareholders and the board. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Last year, this proposal received the votes of a majority of the shares voted for and against. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>The Company&#146;s Statement in Opposition to Proposal No.&nbsp;5 </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Board of Directors recommends a vote AGAINST Proposal No.&nbsp;5. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Board recognizes that executive
compensation is a key corporate governance issue and has carefully considered the proposal and the issues associated with shareholder ratification of executive compensation. While the Board generally supports enhancing the dialogue between
shareholders and the Board, it does not believe that it is in the best interests of the Company&#146;s shareholders to provide for shareholder ratification of executive compensation and recommends a vote against this proposal for the following
reasons. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Compensation Committee of the Board, consisting entirely of independent directors, is responsible for maintaining an
executive compensation program designed to attract, motivate and retain the most highly talented and experienced leadership for the Company. This program is discussed in detail in this Proxy Statement in the section entitled &#147;Executive
Compensation&#151;Compensation Discussion and Analysis.&#148; The program is carefully designed around various components of compensation, including base salaries, incentive bonuses and equity awards, and the Compensation Committee reviews and
approves annually the compensation for all executive officers of the Company. In addition, the Compensation Committee engages an independent compensation consulting firm (see the section entitled &#147;D. Executive Compensation Program Design and
Implementation&#151;5. The Role of Consultants&#148; under &#147;Executive Compensation&#151;Compensation Discussion and Analysis&#148; above) to help it design compensation packages in a manner that effectively serves the interests of the
shareholders by providing appropriate incentives to executive officers and allowing the Company to remain competitive with its peers. Executive compensation practices are influenced by a wide range of complex factors, including changes in strategic
goals, changing economic and industry conditions, accounting requirements and tax laws, evolving governance trends and the competitive compensation practices of other companies. As a result, it is important that the Compensation Committee retain the
flexibility to select the appropriate incentives so that the Company can continue to attract and retain executives of outstanding ability and motivate them to achieve superior performance. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">An advisory vote would not provide the Compensation Committee with any meaningful insight into specific shareholder concerns regarding executive
compensation that it could address when considering the Company&#146;s remuneration policies. Other means of communicating concerns to the Board and/or the Compensation Committee are already available to shareholders. Any shareholder may communicate
specific concerns directly with the Board and/or the Compensation Committee if the shareholder disagrees with the Company&#146;s compensation policies by following the instructions provided in this Proxy Statement in the section entitled </FONT>
</P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">47 </FONT></P>


<p Style='page-break-before:always'>
<HR  SIZE="3" COLOR="#999999" WIDTH="100%" ALIGN="CENTER">

 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px">
<FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">&#147;Communications with the Board&#148; under &#147;Directors&#148; above. This process allows shareholders to voice concerns about executive compensation
before decisions are made, as opposed to merely voting on the results of the decisions. The Annual Meeting also provides a forum for shareholders to enter into a dialogue with the Company on a variety of matters, including executive compensation
issues. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Compensation Committee exercises great care in determining and disclosing executive compensation. The Board believes that an
advisory resolution would not have any legal consequence on any compensation arrangement. Rather, adopting this practice could negatively affect shareholder value by creating the impression among the Company&#146;s executives that their compensation
opportunities could be limited or negatively affected by this practice, and it may very well constrain the Compensation Committee&#146;s efforts to recruit and retain exceptional executives who will focus on the Company&#146;s long-term performance
and results. The Board does not believe the advisory vote will enhance governance practices or improve communication with shareholders, or that it is in the best interest of the Company&#146;s shareholders. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">It is widely expected that the U.S. Congress, in its new session, will enact legislation requiring shareholder advisory votes on executive compensation.
Consequently, it would be premature for the Company to take action at this time to implement a shareholder advisory vote procedure. The Board believes that the Company and its shareholders are best served by monitoring legislative developments and
promptly adopting any new practices related to executive compensation and shareholder advisory votes that are mandated by law or regulation. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman"
SIZE="2">Accordingly, the Board does not believe an advisory vote on executive compensation is in the best interests of the Company and its shareholders and recommends a vote against Proposal No.&nbsp;5. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Vote Required </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The affirmative vote of (i)&nbsp;a
majority of the voting power present or represented by proxy and voting at the Annual Meeting and (ii)&nbsp;a majority of the voting power required to constitute the quorum are required to approve Proposal No.&nbsp;5. </FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>Recommendation of the Board of Directors </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:6px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>The
Board recommends a vote AGAINST the Shareholder Proposal Regarding Advisory Vote on Compensation. </B></FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:24px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2"><B>OTHER MATTERS </B></FONT></P> <P
STYLE="margin-top:12px;margin-bottom:0px; text-indent:4%"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">The Company knows of no other matters to be submitted to the shareholders at the Annual Meeting. If any other matters properly come before the
shareholders at the Annual Meeting, it is the intention of the persons named on the proxy to vote the shares represented thereby on such matters in accordance with their best judgment. </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:18px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT
FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">Dated: January&nbsp;7, 2009 </FONT></P> <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px"><FONT SIZE="1">&nbsp;</FONT></P>
 <P STYLE="margin-top:0px;margin-bottom:0px" ALIGN="center"><FONT FACE="Times New Roman" SIZE="2">48 </FONT></P>
